The Municipal Finance Bureau Reports an Increase in Municipal Treasury Revenue 126

More than 150,000 Yuan Higher than April Last Year

The revenue of the Municipal Treasury of this city has increased significantly this past month compared to the same month last year. According to the statistics released by the Municipal Finance Bureau on the various municipal tax revenues for the past month, important items such as house tax revenue amounted to more than 235,000 yuan, an increase of approximately 59,000 yuan compared to April of the previous year; business tax amounted to more than 109,000 yuan, an increase of more than 51,000 yuan; license tax amounted to more than 235,000 yuan, an increase of more than 31,000 yuan. Other items also showed considerable increases. The total revenue for each item was 607,220.67 yuan, exceeding April of the previous year by 151,239.15 yuan.

The Official and Business Sectors on the Slaughter Tax Issue 127

Differing Opinions

The Municipal Health Bureau's Advice: Reports indicate that the fresh meat industry at the

meeting of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, opposed the levy of slaughter tax, and resolved five items, which are inconsistent with the principles of law and facts. Therefore, we specifically advise adding the following: The slaughter tax is a local tax that is common throughout the country, and has been levied for a long time. When the Jiangsu Provincial Government collected the slaughter tax payable by meat merchants in this city, the meat shops complied and paid it without any objection. Why is it that the municipal government is now collecting it at the original tax rate, but the meat industry is demanding its abolition? The biggest hidden motive in this is that the municipal government has broken the bad system of contractors, and the few meat merchants who jointly contract cannot enjoy the benefits of monopolizing as before. Therefore, they incite colleagues who are unaware of the inside story to rise up in opposition. The Bureau has a few words of advice for the fresh meat shops in the city who do not know the inside story of the contract: (1) The slaughter tax is a local tax that is common throughout the country. By what special status should meat merchants in this city not recognize and pay the legally levied slaughter tax, and they have been paying it for more than ten years? Why have they never raised any objections before? Do they mean that the previous payments were legal, and the current levies are illegal? From the perspective of legal principles and facts, there is no reason for this. (2) Since the slaughter tax is a common local tax, now the Jiangsu Provincial Government has transferred the power to collect this local tax

Page 14

to the local government within its jurisdiction, which is precisely to comply with the central government's resolution to exercise the rules of governance and to prevent the bad habits of division and fragmentation among various agencies. However, the meat merchants took the opportunity of the transfer of collection power by the provincial government to obstruct it. Does this mean that the governance power of the municipal government of this city should always be divided and fragmented, and should always be confused? Moreover, the amount of tax collected is still the same as before, and has not increased by a penny. The meat merchants only need to change from paying the Jiangsu Provincial Government to paying the municipal government according to law. What reason is there to oppose this legitimate measure? From the perspective of legal principles and facts, there is no reason for this. (3) Recruiting merchants to contract tax revenue is one of the evils of the old system. When there is an opportunity to reform it, it should be abolished immediately to prevent the evils of corruption. The city seeks the truth and abolished the slaughter tax contractor system, which is a very legitimate measure. Those with ulterior motives who intend to obstruct this have their own unspeakable secrets. However, they do not distinguish the truth and blindly follow suit, and are used by those with private agendas. This is inevitably foolish and self-indulgent. From the perspective of legal principles and facts, there is no reason for this. As for the five items discussed, their illegality to law and the truth of the facts are as follows: (1) The proposed requirement to abolish the slaughter tax and change it to a business tax, and to pay the original amount before the change, is not feasible. The current slaughter tax levied in this city is still collected at the original tax rate, without any increase. Collecting it by the head is a fair and practical measure. The meat merchants have not increased their burden, so why should they use the contractor's amount as an excuse? The contractor's amount was a contract behavior that the contractor individually signed with the competent authority. The meat merchants have never had a precedent for paying the amount to the competent authority. The so-called original recognized amount is actually unfounded. This is something that all meat merchants should reflect on. (2) The proposed requirement to abolish the technician inspection fee. The meat merchants in each district, in order to set up livestock inspection and slaughtering and sales near their location, voluntarily paid for office expenses. The documents for the voluntary request are all there, and it has been approved by the municipal government. It is not allowed to reverse right and wrong. If the meat merchants in each district can send livestock to the designated places for inspection, this fee can be abolished, which is very much in line with the original intention of the Bureau's regulations. This is something that all meat merchants should reflect on. (3) The request to abolish the pre-slaughter and post-slaughter inspection fees. This inspection fee is not a tax. It is one kind of handling fee. In order to maintain the progress of inspection affairs, and to slightly compensate the needs of municipal public use, it is impossible not to charge this handling fee under the current financial situation of this city. Moreover, this kind of inspection handling fee is stipulated in the municipal regulations of this city, and handling fees are common in all cities. This city still does not have the ability to waive it. This is something that all meat merchants should reflect on. (4) The request to no longer force the purchase of tickets to pay taxes. As mentioned earlier, the slaughter tax should not be avoided, then purchasing tickets to offset the tax payment is a measure that is convenient for investigation and should naturally be in place. Its effect is the same as cash. It is only used to confuse colleagues because of procedural issues, and to make sacrifices for the boycotts of those with ulterior motives. This is too cruel. All meat merchants should quickly reflect on and realize this. (5) The proposed opposition to the municipal government's construction of slaughterhouses. May I ask, what is the direct relationship between the municipal government taking over the slaughter tax and planning to build new slaughterhouses? It is far-fetched and discussed together, which shows that those who instigate trouble are doing everything possible. The reasons why the city should build a municipal slaughterhouse have been detailed in the plan. Due to space limitations, and recognizing that this kind of talk is getting farther and farther away, it is temporarily unnecessary to correct it. Let me give a few examples to ask questions: Should the sheds in Zhabei be allowed to exist forever? Or should they be gradually rebuilt into public housing as the current municipal government is doing? Should the narrow alleys be narrow forever? Or should they be gradually rebuilt as they are now? If it is said that these sheds and narrow places should be rebuilt, then the dark, narrow, and foul-smelling slaughtering should be eliminated, and a clean and well-proportioned slaughterhouse should be built. There is no reason to object to this. Advocating opposition only reveals the weakness of one's understanding. This is something that all meat merchants should reflect on. This is a special advice. I hope you will know this and not be deceived again.

The Claims of the Various Industries Tax Rules Association: The various industries of this city

The Tax Rules Research Committee of the Industry Guilds yesterday presented a document to the Municipal Government regarding the collection of slaughter tax by the Municipal Government, requesting that it be changed to a business tax. The document states, "Submitting a request to change the slaughter tax to a business tax, hoping that you will examine and order compliance. According to the letter from the Fresh Meat Industry Guild, it is reported by a majority of colleagues that since the fourth year of the Republic, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance collected slaughter tax in various districts, each fresh pig had to pay a tax of four jiao, plus an educational surtax of four fen. After the collection was managed by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education in the 17th year of the Republic, a health inspection fee of one jiao was added. However, this tax was only collected in the urban areas of the north and south of the city, and not in the concessions. Therefore, the colleagues in the inland areas feel very painful compared to the colleagues in the concessions. Now that the central government has issued an order for the provinces to abolish transit duties, and all local miscellaneous taxes must be exempted, this slaughter tax is one of the miscellaneous taxes, and according to central regulations, it should naturally be abolished. We originally hoped that the central government would issue an order to exempt it to reduce the burden. Unexpectedly, we saw in the newspapers yesterday that the Shanghai Municipal Government still wants to collect it. If it is implemented, it will be difficult to maintain our business and livelihood. Therefore, we request you to forward the matter to the higher authorities to withdraw the order and maintain our livelihood, and we will be extremely grateful." Based on this, in order to protect the interests of our colleagues, we should forward the situation to the central government and show concern for the difficulties of businesses, and issue an order to abolish the slaughter tax in Shanghai, so as to show compassion. Reading the reports in the newspaper in recent days, the slaughter tax of the industry is voluntarily paid by colleagues, but recently the government has ordered it to be collected according to the head, which has caused panic and endless appeals. Reading Article 6 of the General Outline of Business Tax Collection in Various Provinces issued by the Ministry, it stipulates that after the implementation of the business tax, the original slaughter tax in various provinces should be abolished. Now that the implementation of the business tax in this city is imminent, it seems unnecessary to change it again at this extremely urgent time, so as to avoid panic and appeals from businessmen in the industry. The tax rate of the slaughter tax cannot be evenly distributed in the Chinese concession area, and it is especially necessary to change it to a business tax. With the letter in front of us, we should prepare a document and forward it to you, hoping that you will examine it and order the Finance Bureau to change the slaughter tax to a business tax. Before the business tax is implemented, it should be paid according to the original amount, so as to avoid changes and be in accordance with the law, which is fair and convenient."

Various Industries Tax Rules Association Cables Requesting the Abolition of Sand and Gravel Management Fees 130

The Various Industries Tax Rules Committee of this city specifically telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to abolish the sand and gravel management fee, stating: "Ministry of Finance of the National Government of Nanjing, according to the letter from the Sand and Gravel Industry Guild, the sand and mud operated by the members of the association are taken from the sea sand of the deserted islands of Ningbo and the silt sand of Huzhou in the mainland, and transported to Shanghai for building purposes, which is actually using waste to help people's livelihood and can also dredge rivers and clear waterways. As for the boatmen who take sand and mud from the place of origin, they pay land price to the local government office according to regulations, two fen per ton, and pay education donations and police fees, etc. After hiring small workers to dig, transport, and load the boats to Shanghai, they hire barges to transship, rely on the shore to hire small workers to unload, load trucks and transport to the destination. Statistics show that the selling price is only two yuan per ton, which is not to take value from the substance, but to seek compensation for the wages of laborers and the boatmen's water feet, the barge's barge fees, and the numbers are run by merchants, pay for the accounts of upper and lower merchants, and the commission for each ton is only one jiao, which is a transfer agent for customers. Over time, for decades, the government has given care to workers and does not levy taxes. Unexpectedly, just now we are in the time of abolishing transit duties and eliminating excessive taxes, there is the establishment of a sand and mud production and sales tax authority by the Construction Department of the Zhejiang Provincial Government. The amount of tax is as high as more than fifty percent, and the name is cleverly established as management fee and production tax. Two companies, Dachang and Yitai, contract to set up collection offices in Shanghai, which are commissioned by the Construction Department of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, and issue sand transportation permits at the office. It is found that branch posts have been set up in Wusong and other places to secretly release patrol boats, which patrol day and night. The penalties are extremely harsh. I have checked the transit duties system, which has hurt merchants and harmed the country for a long time. The National Government is determined to abolish it in order to show compassion for the difficulties of businesses, and the Ministry of Finance telegraphed on March 22 to announce to the whole country to clear away the accumulated malpractices in order to completely eradicate the accumulated ills and benefit the people. All industries congratulated each other. Only our sand and gravel industry suffered heavy taxes during this transit duty abolition period, which runs counter to the National Government's intention to show compassion for the difficulties of businesses. Complying with the clear order, the compensation after the abolition of transit duties is to change to business tax. According to the regulations of Article 4 of the General Outline of Business Tax, the business tax rate should be calculated by the thousandth method according to the taxable standard, and should not exceed two per thousand at most, which can already prove that the tax levied after the abolition of transit duties is the business tax that should not exceed two per thousand, and all other similar transit taxes in disguise cannot continue to exist. To prove it again, according to the old tariff outline, sand and gravel are one of the four essential needs for building houses, roads, and embankments for the people's livelihood, and their tax is specially allowed to be exempted. Now, for the sand and mud that we sell for two yuan per ton, which is the cost of labor, we suddenly add a tax of one yuan per ton, which is as high as fifty percent. Even if transit duties are abolished and taxes are added, it cannot be so much. This is obviously a case of cunning merchants deceiving higher authorities in order to seek profit. Managing sand and mud by setting up a bureau will lead to others following suit and affecting other industries. After celebrating the abolition of transit duties, we suffer heavy taxes. If the members of the industry suffer this heavy burden, the livelihood of 40,000 to 50,000 people in the city who rely on this life will be plunged into despair. Therefore, we urgently present this matter, hoping that you will forward it to the Jiang Zhe Provincial Government according to reason, and request that it be clearly ordered to abolish the excessive tax in order to relieve the people's difficulties and show compassion for businesses. It is said that the abolition of excessive taxes is one of the Party's internal affairs policies, and the Central Government has a great determination to abolish transit duties. However, the Zhejiang Provincial Government has a sand and gravel management fee production tax in disguise in the form of transit duties when the Central Government abolished transit duties. The tax rate reaches more than fifty percent, which not only violates the political program, but also goes against the intention of abolishing transit duties. Moreover, the contractor system has long been abolished, and the tax is still contracted by Dachang and Yitai companies, which is even more disrespectful to government orders. It is even more shocking to establish a tax collection agency of the Zhejiang Provincial Government within the Shanghai area. Moreover, according to item 2 of the draft business tax rate in Shanghai, the sand and gravel industry is taxed at two per thousand, and it seems that there cannot be an illegal overcharge in addition to the burden of business tax. What reasons does the Zhejiang Provincial Government use to set up the sand and gravel management fee production tax? It is difficult to understand. I read in the newspaper that the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Finance collected a five percent stone donation in Yinxian, authorized to the contractor. Zhang Caizheng, the Deputy Minister of Finance, immediately sent a letter requesting the abolition and punished the Yinxian County Governor. Reading today's newspaper, the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Finance has replied by telegram ordering the abolition by the Department. Then the nature of the sand and gravel management fee production tax of the bureau is the same, and the heavy tax is even more serious. According to reason, we should send a telegram to request and order the Zhejiang Provincial Government to abolish it immediately, so as to relieve the difficulties of businesses and maintain government orders. In fact, it is public convenience. The Tax Rules Research Committee of the Shanghai Industry Guilds, Han, (Note: Some of the oil prints are unclear and cannot be corrected)

Woman Brutally Murdered in Eastern Hotel in the City 132

The man she arrived with left in the middle of the night

The horrifying scene was discovered at noon

A bloody channel with a hatchet on the bed

The fatal wounds were on the jaw and neck

On the 13th, at 4 PM, a man and a woman arrived at the Eastern Hotel on Minguo Road, Xiaodongmen, in the Nanshi district. They booked room number 38 on the third floor. The porter asked them to write their names, ages, and hometowns in the registration book. The man wrote his name as Wei Jinhuo, age 30, local. The woman was referred to as his family member. The man appeared to be older than 30, wearing a blue-lined cotton padded jacket and pants, and a duckbill cap. He was thin and tall, with a physique resembling that of a smoker. The woman was nearly 30, with a long face and a slender figure. Her hair was cut short, not reaching her shoulders. She wore a black coat, black stockings, and black satin round-mouth shoes. After the room was booked, they paid the room fee of one dollar and twenty cents as usual. Half an hour later, the man and woman went out together and did not return until 12 midnight. The woman was no longer wearing her coat. They went to bed soon after. At that time, Zhang Gensheng, the night shift porter of the hotel, was on duty and had not slept. The porter's desk was located in front of room number 38. At 3:30 AM (yesterday morning), the man opened the door and went out. The porter did not suspect anything because people from the fish market in Xiaodongmen often booked rooms and had to get up in the middle of the night. Furthermore, the outside of the room was a brick wall, and no sound was heard from inside. Until noon yesterday, at 12 PM, the porter knocked on the door, thinking that if it was past noon, the room fee would be calculated for two days. He shouted for the people inside to get up, but there was no response. He knocked on the door for a long time, but there was no sound. He became suspicious and opened the door with a key. He couldn't help but cry out because the woman had been hacked to death on the bed. He immediately reported to the manager, Chu Lianke, who went to investigate. The woman's body was lying face down on the bed, facing outward. There was a channel of blood on the bed, and a hatchet (the kind used in red wood workshops) was next to her head. There were also bloody handprints on the account. The body was still covered with a quilt, and the curtains were drawn. Chu Lianke immediately reported to the 2nd Precinct of the 1st District, which sent patrol officers to investigate. The Public Security Bureau sent an inspector to the scene to inquire. Chu Lianke then submitted a report to the local court for an autopsy. Prosecutor Wu Shixin, along with recorder Qian Yinpei, coroner Xuan Zhiming, and bailiff Xu Guoguang, arrived at the scene. The autopsy revealed that the woman's corpse was about twenty years old. She was wearing a white cloth undershirt and pants. Her shoes and socks were on the floor. Her wool shirt and pants had been taken away by the murderer. Her right front tooth was a gold tooth. Her eyes were sunken, her tongue was extended, her hands were bent, and her feet were straight. There were two fatal wounds, one on her jaw and one on her neck, slightly to the right. There were also two non-fatal wounds, one on the back of her right hand and one on her left shoulder. It was suspected that the deceased was sleeping at the time and was killed by someone straddling her. They immediately filled out the autopsy report, took photographs, and ordered the Sixteen Shops Landlord to collect the body. Chu Lianke was instructed to take the porter Zhang Gensen to the court this afternoon for questioning to assist in the arrest of the murderer. The murder weapon, shoes, and socks were taken as evidence and stored in the warehouse. According to this case, the murderer was definitely the man. It is speculated that the cause must be impulse.

American Soldiers Stealing and Selling Handguns 133

Selling to Russians who resold to Chinese

The investigation was discovered through donation and inspection licenses

A number of soldiers from the U.S. Marine Corps stationed in Shanghai are billeted at the barracks at 116 Xinzha Road. One of the soldiers, named Eiworthsen, took advantage of the company commander's absence from the camp on the 25th of last month. He secretly entered his room, opened the drawer with a key, and stole a handgun from the iron box. Two days later, he took advantage of another opportunity to steal another gun. The performance of these handguns is far beyond what ordinary firearms can compare with, so the value of the two guns is worth 300 taels of gold. However, the marine regarded it as a piece of junk. Later, through the introduction of Simmermand of the same company, he sold it to Leibkovich, a Russian at 26 Carter Road, for 195 yuan. Later, the company commander discovered that guns were missing, but he didn't know who stole them. So he reported it to the police station, asking for an investigation. A few days ago, a person surnamed Li asked a friend surnamed Wu to bring a gun to the police station to donate and get a self-defense gun license. The Western officer inspected the Western text and serial number engraved on the handle of the gun, all of which had been destroyed, leaving only traces. After investigating the origin of the gun, it was learned that it was purchased from Leibkovich, who obtained it from the two American soldiers. So the competent company commander was notified, and the two soldiers were arrested. After questioning, they confessed. The police station immediately sent Chinese and Western detectives to arrest the Russian and found the remaining gun. Wu was dismissed. Yesterday morning, the Russian was escorted to the Special District Local Court and charged with violating Article 2 of the Regulations for the Suppression of Military Firearms and Receiving Stolen Goods. The U.S. military camp also escorted the two soldiers to the court as evidence. They confessed that when they sold the guns, they had told the Russian that they were firearms used by the U.S. Navy. Judge Wu Tingqi questioned the defendant, who insisted that the two soldiers were not wearing uniforms when they were peddling the guns and did not say that they were military firearms, so he bought them. The judge ordered the defendant to be detained pending further investigation. The two American soldiers were escorted back to the military camp by the company commander to await trial.

Songhu Branch Line to Reduce Ticket Prices 134

Between Tiantong'an and Jiangwan

After the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway's Songhu branch line increased the ticket price between Tiantong'an and Jiangwan stations from five cents to one dime, the number of passengers has decreased significantly. This is because there are public buses operating on this section, and the bus fare is only 23 copper coins, and it can go directly to Jiangwan Town, which is more convenient than taking the train. Therefore, in the past, most passengers abandoned the train and took the bus instead. It is now heard that the railway bureau intends to reduce the ticket price between Tiantong'an and Jiangwan to facilitate passengers, and it will be implemented soon.

Mr. Szigeti's Performance Tonight 137

Women's Temperance Association Held Delegates' Discussion Meeting Yesterday 138

Reporting on the progress of association affairs in various regions

The Chinese Women's Temperance Association held its second national delegates' discussion meeting at the Yipinxiang Hotel yesterday. Representatives from the capital, Zhenjiang, Suzhou, Shandong, and other provinces and cities were present. Mrs. Zheng Yangxiu, the chairman, first reported on the situation of membership in various regions and sent a congratulatory telegram to the National Assembly. Then, they commemorated the martyrs Ding Yihua, Liu Luodaiqing, Ma Zugan, Ou Bai, Yang Jingshi, and Li Peisheng, ladies, in a moment of silence. Then, they declared, "The purpose of this association is to make people restrain from all wasteful activities such as smoking, drinking, and gambling. It bears a great mission. Today, representatives from various branches are here to discuss good ways of temperance to achieve our goals." Then, the representative from Nanjing reported on the association's affairs, saying that they had recently carried out four tasks: (1) contacting young women in Nanjing to arouse their interest in the association's work and ideals; (2) starting to select materials and edit textbooks; (3) doing medical and hygiene work for poor women in nearby thatched huts; (4) recruiting members and organizing committees. The association has four goals: (1) not to hope to do great things or talk empty words, but to do some small things practically; (2) to be willing to move people with work, not with ideals; (3) to start from the near and do things from the small to the large, step by step; (4) to do the most with the most economical methods. Then, the representative from Ningbo Mirror reported on the association's affairs, saying that it is important to engage in written publicity to praise the importance of abstinence, and to use general students to work in the association's affairs. Then, representatives from Hudong, Huzhou, and Jiujiang reported on the association's affairs in succession, saying that they are working hard to promote it to the villagers and the public to let them know the benefits of abstinence, and to let students persuade relatives and friends not to smoke or drink alcohol, and to run people's schools and workers' night schools to instill knowledge. The representatives from Guangdong and Beiping did not have time to report due to time constraints. After the reports were finished, it was already past 4 o'clock. The directors and affairs department opened a welcome meeting for representatives from various branches, followed by a banquet. After dinner, Ms. Liu Wang Liming gave a speech on the local contribution of the association in ten years, which was quite poignant.

Recruiting New Members for the Shanghai North District Security Corps 139

The third team of the Shanghai North District Security Corps has a long history, well-trained skills, high morale, a close-knit organization, and strict discipline. It has always been known as the champion. It is heard that the team's original volunteer members have served for three years and have been retired to the reserve force in accordance with the regulations, so there is an urgent need to recruit new members. It is heard that the procedures for joining the team are very simple. Anyone who is in the Shanghai North District, is interested in protecting the community, is between the ages of twenty and thirty, is in good health, can endure hardship, has no bad habits, has a proper occupation, and has a solid local shop guarantee can report to the team headquarters at Baoshan Road, Baoshanli, Zhabei, at any time before the 31st of this month. It is also heard that the team has a limited number of vacancies this time, and the recruitment will be closed after the quota is filled, and no extensions will be made.

Murder on the Xinjiangtian Ship 140

The murderer has been sent to the Ningbo Court

The union is in negotiations

The Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Ningbo liner Xinjiangtian returned to Shanghai from Ningbo yesterday. There was a tragic case of murder on board caused by a fight between a waiter and a carpenter. The reporter received a report from a passenger on the ship and went to investigate the details of the incident from all parties. The details are recorded as follows: Gambling Fight: The Xinjiangtian ship specializes in the Shanghai-Ningbo route. At 5 PM on the 12th, it departed from Shanghai. At about 7 PM, while sailing in the Sanjia Water area, waiters, carpenters, coppersmiths, sailors, and others gathered in the coppersmith's room to play Pai Gow. The carpenter Jiang Amao bet one yuan, and a waiter bet two yuan. At that time, everyone wanted to compete to see the cards and sit at the door. The two refused to give in to each other, which led to a quarrel. First, they argued, then they wrestled, but unexpectedly, it led to a tragic disaster of murder. Carpenter Injured: During the fight, the carpenter Jiang Amao from Fenghua was held by a waiter, who then punched him hard. The order was chaotic for a while. Later, sailors and others stepped forward to separate the two. The waiter was still unwilling and wanted to fight the carpenter again, but was stopped by the sailors. After being twisted and beaten by a waiter, Jiang Amao returned to his cabin to rest. Because of injuries to his chest and waist, he was in unbearable pain. He called his foster son, (14 years old, working as a waiter on the ship), to the room to massage him. Sudden Death: Not long after Jiang Amao returned to his room, purple marks appeared on his chest, and his breathing was not smooth. His foster son stroked his body, but it was ineffective. He felt more severe pain and discomfort in his waist and abdomen. Colleagues suspected it was acute cholera and called someone in the ship who could relieve Sha to treat him. Unexpectedly, around 11 PM at night, when the person who pricked Sha came to the room, Jiang had already died. It was less than four hours from the fight. Murderer Sent to the Bureau: After Jiang died, his foster son reported it to the chief mate and the captain, who placed the murderer, a waiter, under custody, and waited until dawn (the 13th) when the ship arrived in Ningbo to report to the customs. The customs sent a doctor to inspect the ship, and the deceased's body showed purple and black swelling, which was obviously caused by beating. The murderer was sent to the Public Security Bureau and transferred to the court for judicial trial. The deceased's body was also moved ashore. Court Inspection: After accepting the case, the court first sent someone to inspect the deceased Jiang Amao. The chest, abdomen, waist, and other parts were covered with black swelling, which was obviously caused by external injuries. After re-examining the internal organs, there were no injuries, and the sudden death was also very suspicious. The murderer, the waiter, was first detained, and then the body was prepared for coffin collection, and his family was notified. After they came to Ningbo from Fenghua, the case will be opened for trial. Union Negotiation: Yesterday, when the ship arrived in Shanghai, the shipowner reported to the General Administration that the carpenter and waiter were both in the union, and this matter had nothing to do with the administration, and had nothing to do with the bureau, so it was operating as usual. However, the carpenter had reported this matter to the Junan Association and asked for an appeal, while the waiter had also reported to the union and asked for assistance, saying that this case was very bizarre, and the external injuries alone were not necessarily fatal. Please help to clarify the injustice. The two trade unions are in negotiations on this matter.

Dr. Wade, a world expert on leprosy, gave a lecture yesterday afternoon at 4 PM at the invitation of the Shanghai Women's Support Association of the China Leprosy Relief Association. In the evening, he attended a banquet hosted by the China Leprosy Relief Association. Leprosy was considered incurable a few years ago, but in fact, it was because treatment was too late, so the treatment period had passed. It was already past 10 o'clock when the meeting was dismissed. It was also heard that Mr. Wade attended the Rotary Club lecture yesterday. This Sunday afternoon at 5 PM, he will give a lecture at the Chinese YMCA and show a film on leprosy work. At that time, people from all walks of life can go to listen to the lecture.

Housing Dispute in Bao'an Fang, French Concession 143

Landlord Pretends to Repair, Orders Tenants to Evacuate

Tenants Meet to Plan Unified Response

The Bao'an Fang houses on Bauer Road in the French Concession, totaling more than 40 buildings, are owned by the Bao'an Real Estate Company. The houses are only eight years old and look brand new. In April of this year, the landlord suddenly notified the tenants that they would be "undergoing major repairs" starting on May 5th and demanded that all tenants vacate by the end of April. Upon hearing this news, all the tenants were panicked, believing that the houses were brand new and did not need major repairs. Even if minor repairs were needed, there was no need to demand that all tenants evacuate. Therefore, they unanimously expressed their opposition and negotiated with the landlord, requesting that they withdraw the order to force them to evacuate. However, the landlord ignored them and sent people to notify the tenants to vacate within the deadline, otherwise the construction would begin. The entire tenant community, due to ineffective requests, convened a general meeting yesterday afternoon at 1 PM to discuss countermeasures. All the tenants arrived and elected Xu Zhiming as chairman. After reporting, the tenants expressed their opinions one after another and decided as follows: (1) The landlord is using repairs as an excuse to force tenants to evacuate. This kind of action may have other intentions and we vow to oppose it to the death. (2) Officially establish a tenants' union. (3) Elect Xu Zhiming, Yuan Zhuoren, and Peng Buqing as representatives to be responsible for handling negotiations. (4) The Tenants' Union will first submit a written reply to the landlord, asking them to withdraw the order immediately. (5) Submit a petition to the municipal government, the municipal party department, the Social Affairs Bureau, and the French Concession Taxpayers Association to uphold justice and provide assistance. (6) Issue a declaration seeking unified assistance from all walks of life. (7) All tenants unite and resolutely use all their strength to deal with the situation, no matter what. (8) If necessary, hire a lawyer to protect their rights according to the law. The meeting adjourned after the resolutions.

Investigated 54 Cases in the Past Year

Abuse is Divided into Twelve Categories

The Protection Department of the China Child Welfare Association carries out its work in five sections: investigation, statistics, propaganda, communication, and relief. The investigation work is particularly busy. It has investigated 54 cases in the past year, distributed among twelve types of abuse, such as 13 cases of beating with sticks, 4 cases of kicking and punching, 5 cases of hunger and imprisonment, 1 case of stabbing with cones and rope binding, 5 cases of abandonment and lack of education, 7 cases of luring and selling into prostitution, 1 case of superstition and killing of children, 11 cases of child labor, 1 case of needle piercing the mouth and scalding the back with water, 1 case of burning and scalding with red-hot iron objects, 3 cases of cruel magic tricks, and 2 cases of being run over by a car and drowning. It is heard that the department also wants to thoroughly study the motives for abuse and the methods adopted to carry out fundamental prevention.

The Ministry of Finance believes that tax evasion by cigarette merchants in the concession is unavoidable. Because both cases still need to be investigated, the counterfeiting case was rescheduled for this Saturday, and the tax evasion case was postponed to the next session. It is heard that if tax evasion is discovered, according to the regulations, a fine of 30 times the amount of tax evaded will be imposed, which can be said to be severe.

Tang Yi's Telegram to Deng, Lin, Xiao, and Gu 153

Guangzhou inquiry: Deng Zeru, Lin Zichao, Xiao Focheng, Gu Xiangqin, esteemed sirs, I have recently read in the newspapers your telegram of the 30th, pointing out the shortcomings of current affairs, ostensibly impeaching officials, and listing my humble name, making baseless attacks. I have considered it repeatedly, but I cannot understand the reason. Since the rise of the Northern Expeditionary Army, the reason why I, Yi, have never uttered a word or offered a suggestion is not for any other reason. I believe that the foundation for the success of the revolution lies in unity and the avoidance of division. If those who discuss politics are so eager to express their own opinions that they do not take the time to choose carefully, they will inevitably end up supporting the warlords and losing their original purpose. Therefore, I have been constantly anxious and uneasy, and have taken inaction as the guiding principle, and have not wavered from this course for several years. However, during my time in Tianjin, some people accused me of being a reactionary and regarded me as having obvious bad records. In recent years, residing in Shanghai, you gentlemen have compared me to those who are engaged in behind-the-scenes activities and regarded me as holding an important position. If there are no such actions, how can there be bad records? I have never held office, so how can there be any important position? The previous discussion is self-evident and needs no further debate. Let me concede a point and speak of recent events. It may be that the telegram with your signatures was written by a secretary or based on hearsay from afar. Even if there are inaccuracies, it would not be a burden. However, the accusations of wrongdoing against me are extremely insulting and cannot be accepted by Yi. I am now briefly recounting past events to inform you gentlemen and await your judgment. Although Yi's conduct and abilities may be lacking, he has his own standing in the history of the Republic of China's revolution. Since the founding of the Republic of China, with the establishment of the Kuomintang, Yi's dedication to the Party's political department and its organs, and his ideals, have been clearly revealed. From the meeting of representatives of various provinces in the Xinhai Revolution to the Nanjing Senate and then the National Assembly, I have served in succession, and what I have expressed is generally known to those who are slightly familiar with national affairs. Mr. Lin Zichao was even someone I spent time with day and night. What exactly did I do to oppose the Party, and when did I do it? Please tell me. This is the first point. When the National Assembly was restored in the sixth year of the Republic of China, comrades within the Party were divided into small groups to engage in the distribution of cabinet positions or the hunting of other official posts. Yi was unwilling to do so. I took it upon myself to complete the constitutional work, and because the procedures for discussing the constitution were strict and required a two-thirds majority to pass, I had to remain neutral and mediate. Therefore, I did not join any small organization, and this was not accidental. I still remember that during the period of the Constitutional Protection Movement, the Political Study Clique's autocracy reached its extreme in the ninth year of the Republic of China. Because Yi had previously advocated reconciliation and caused misunderstandings, I had no choice but to admit defeat and resolutely withdraw. Later, when the military government was reorganized for the second time, comrades in Guangdong resolved to adopt several articles of debarment measures. Therefore, all suspected elements were placed on the list of those to be excluded, but there was no accusation against Yi. I ask you gentlemen today, if you insist on adding my humble name to the end of the Political Study Clique and then be happy, what have you seen that makes you say so? This is the second point. After the ninth year of the Republic of China, Yi resided in Shanghai until May of the eleventh year, when the National Assembly reconvened and I went north. In May of the twelfth year, I declared my intention to go south again due to opposition to bribery in elections. After the fourteenth year of the Republic of China, when the National Assembly became ineffective, although I resided in Pingjin for a long time, I did not associate with any warlords. If I had any contact with them, it was only in the course of my official duties. Aside from attending meetings, I have not been an official for a single day in the past twenty years. The so-called dependence on warlords may be true of other comrades who have missions and have other secret intentions, or there may be some suspicious signs. I did not expect you gentlemen to rashly make such a comparison to Yi. This is the third point. As for the writings I have published over the years, apart from those denouncing the usurpation of power by warlords, opposing bribery in elections, and advocating for various issues related to the Southwestern Constitutional Protection Movement, there are also articles discussing the constitution and the provincial constitution related to the national constitution. Looking back now, I may regret some of my early works, but at the time, they were generally approved by a majority of comrades. Moreover, the disclosure of my advocacy for provincial constitutions occurred long before the announcement of the Prime Minister's Outline of National Reconstruction. How could it be considered a defamation? This is the fourth point. In summary, I have briefly presented here my past words and deeds and my recent attitude, which should be judged by the public. I have previously seen some small newspapers in Shanghai occasionally publish inaccurate reports, and I have often dismissed them with a smile, thinking that the younger generation is unfamiliar with my life and does not understand the past, and often writes hastily, falsely accusing their predecessors. It seemed that there was no need to correct them one by one. I did not expect that such fallacies would spread without end. Your gentlemen's telegram even included them in your accusations. Future generations will view the present as the present views the past. Therefore, I dare not spare words to correct them, to seek your wise judgment and to show it to those who come after. I have presented my thoughts frankly, hoping for your kind understanding. Tang Yi respectfully submits.

Zhang Hu Narrates Debt Lawsuit 154

Former Finance Minister Zhang Hu arrived in Shanghai last night. When someone inquired about the debt lawsuit in Beijing, Zhang said that he had entrusted Zhang Jinji Lumber Mill to build a house in Tianjin, but because the project did not conform to the contract, about two or three thousand yuan of the final payment had not been paid. While I was in Tianjin, Zhang Jinji filed a lawsuit in Beiping. Now I hear that I am traveling south, they have followed me here and sued me in the Jiangning Local Court. I, respecting the court, personally went to court, only answered a few questions and then withdrew, and there was no detention overnight. The capital is nearby, and it is self-evident. I am sincerely afraid that friends from afar will misunderstand, so I am stating the truth here.

Settlement of Wage Arrears for Employees of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Ships 157

The wage strike of the four wharf workers of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has been resolved through the mediation of Section Chief Shen Zhongyi and others. The wage strike of the sailors on various ships has also been calmed down. The sailors on the company's ships were owed a total of two or three months' wages. The former administration issued checks for two or three months' wages, but upon maturity, they could not be cashed, resulting in a check bouncing dispute. At this time, the bureau members received a bonus of one and a half months' salary. The sailors on the various ships were greatly dissatisfied, believing that those who risked their lives in the wind and waves were still owed wages, while the land-based staff were comfortably receiving bonuses. They decided to go on strike unanimously. Che Defang, the director of the All-Safety Association, earnestly persuaded the members and, at the same time, represented them to the bureau, requesting the new commissioner to expedite the payment of the arrears. After two days and nights of tireless persuasion, he pleaded with the sailors to consider the overall situation and not to go on strike for the arrears owed by the former administration at the beginning of the new commissioner's term. Che Defang shuttled between labor and management, tirelessly enduring complaints. On the 12th, the bureau cashed the wage arrears checks. Che ordered the water and medical officers of each ship to instruct the workers to resume work and set sail as usual. After the wages were issued, people were sent by car to deliver them to the ships en route. The matter was resolved satisfactorily, and the strike wave on the various ships subsided invisibly. As for the wage arrears for April, they will be issued when the ships return to Shanghai. Mr. Che also prevented the workers from issuing a declaration requesting social judgment on the wage arrears case, and did not allow it to be published.

Awaiting mediation by the Social Bureau

More than 2,000 workers from 140 local Chinese and Western bookbinding companies, including Ma Hongji, went on strike. Workers from Mao Haoji on Xiangshan Road and Xie Feng on Zhiyuan Road violated the discipline and were destroyed by the crowd. The Public Security Bureau has dispatched police to protect them.

Book Industry Meeting: The Bookbinding Industry Trade Association previously dispatched Ding Handong and Xu Hanqing with letters to the Book Industry Trade Association, requesting a 40% increase in book prices. Yesterday, the association replied, "Regarding the letter from your association requesting a 40% increase in bookbinding prices for bookbinding workers, we have learned that our industry has been facing increased costs and sluggish business in recent years, and we are unable to increase prices. In addition to inviting the industry to meet again at 4:00 PM on the 16th to discuss, we will reply first. Please note."

Statistics on Workers' Wages and Working Hours in This City 159

Disclosed by the Municipal Social Bureau

This city has never had comprehensive wage statistics. If there are any, they started with the "Shanghai Wages and Working Hours in 1929" compiled by the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau. The bureau investigated more than 20 important industries in this city, with 2,326 factories and a total of 285,700 workers. It took a year to complete the compilation. The content is divided into three parts: Part 1, Compilation Method of Wage and Working Hour Statistics, discusses in detail the types of wage statistics, the sources of wage statistics, business classification, job classification, wage index, and compilation method of working hour statistics, etc. Part 2, Wage Rate and Working Hour Statistics in 1929, contains an analysis of the number of factories and workers in this city, and the average wage rate and working hour materials for each industry are very rich and accurate. Part 3, Statistics on Actual Income of Workers in 1929, examines in detail the reasons for the monthly changes in the average number. Mr. Kong Xiangxi of the Ministry of Industry wrote in the preface, "The enumeration is comprehensive and profound, and the insights are thorough. The publication of this book will greatly benefit the people of the country." Mr. Raymond Moley of the New York Social Research Science Institute in the United States wrote in the preface, "This report can be said to be a practical attempt to study the problems caused by modern industry, striving to seek facts and describe them." Professor Lampard of Shanghai University wrote in the preface, "This kind of factual truth is the result of research conducted with a fair attitude and scientific methods." In addition, Mr. Chen Changheng and Mr. Chen Huayin of the Legislative Yuan, and Mr. Cai Zhengya, who was in charge of this project, also have prefaces to introduce the book. The book is published by the Commercial Press.

Effective at the End of the Month

The Zi Lin News reports that, according to customs news, Mr. Mai, the Commissioner of the Jianghai Customs in this port, will be transferred to Qingdao to become the Commissioner of the Jiaohai Customs, and Mr. Lao, the Commissioner of the Jiaohai Customs, will be transferred here, effective at the end of this month. When Commissioner Mei was promoted to the position of Inspector General of Customs, Mr. Mai succeeded him and has held the position ever since. Municipal Chamber of Commerce Urges All Industries to Switch to Chinese Insurance 163

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to all industry associations yesterday, urging them to refuse foreign insurance in the future and switch to insurance companies established by Chinese nationals. The letter reads, "We received a letter from the All-Circles Aid to Xinhaishan Committee on the 12th of this month, stating that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Xinxin ship encountered a reef and was wrecked en route in 1928, and all the goods on board were lost. Among them, the goods of 55 merchants, including the Minbang Hengyu, had been insured with foreign insurance companies, but after the incident, the companies made excuses to refuse compensation. After the judicial authorities made a judgment, they repeatedly stalled, intending to evade responsibility. Such behavior is not only due to the lack of integrity and morality of foreign merchants, but also an excellent technique of economic aggression by imperialists. If we do not allow ourselves to be fooled, we should refuse to insure with foreign insurance companies in the future. Those who have already insured should withdraw the insurance upon expiration and switch to insurance companies founded by Chinese nationals. Then, similar incidents will not happen again, and the outflow of rights and interests can be recovered in case of emergency. Therefore, at the All-Circles Meeting on the Xinhaishan Case held in this city on April 28, a temporary motion was made by the Sanshan Guild Hall, requesting that all chambers of commerce across the country and all industry associations in this city be notified to refuse insurance with foreign companies in order to prevent future troubles, and it was unanimously passed. We are sending this letter to you to do as requested. In order to ensure that compensation disputes are easily protected in the future, the members of each guild should be ordered to switch to domestic insurance companies for fire and water insurance. If there are any restrictions that have not yet expired, they should be switched to domestic insurance as soon as they expire. If it is limited by facts and domestic insurance companies cannot accommodate all of them, they should also switch to companies that comply with our country's legal jurisdiction. This is related to the commercial interests of each industry, so you must pay attention to it in advance to avoid regrets."

Another Discussion on the Qianzhuang Law 164

Zhou Yangwen's Reply to Mr. Gu Youdao

Zhou Yangwen's reply to Mr. Gu Youdao on the necessity of the Qianzhuang Law states, "I recently read the submission to the Wuchen Society in Shen Bao, which reprinted Mr. Gu Youdao, a reporter from the Qianye Monthly, on my article "Is the Qianzhuang Law Necessary?" published on May 1. His many arguments show that the interest of the people of the country in the concept of the rule of law is growing stronger, which is a cause for celebration. In summary, the main points of Mr. Gu's paper are: (1) The buying and selling of silver and the import and export of taxes are a type of handling fee for the qianzhuang industry. (2) Credit lending was able to meet the needs of the entire society in the past. (3) Credit lending is a kind of morality. (4) Under the party rule of curbing capital, one should not focus solely on those with capital. (5) Take the silk cocoon and rice lending as an example. Regarding the first point, Mr. Gu has already admitted that it should not exist. He has also admitted the principle of the second point, but questioned that mortgage lending today cannot meet the needs of the entire society. According to the original text of my book, there are many methods of lending, and by using them flexibly, they can not only meet the needs of the entire society, but also help with the people's livelihood. Moreover, they are all beneficial to the industry and commerce that have been established and newly established by the current financial industry, such as the expansion of bill discounting, the verification of goods procurement, etc., which are also included. Unfortunately, Mr. Gu did not have time to examine them in detail. As for the third point, recognizing credit lending as a kind of morality is to directly recognize the financial industry as a charitable organization. The understanding seems to be wrong. Moreover, credit lending has the principle of credit lending. According to the principle of credit lending, there are three major elements: (1) financial resources, (2) ability, and (3) credit. The three are indispensable. If there is financial resources but no credit, then the clearing of creditor's rights and debts will never be straightforward. If there is credit and ability but no financial resources, then it will inevitably lead to being willing but unable to do so. If there is financial resources and credit but no ability, then the career will inevitably fail. However, the number of people in the world who can fully possess these three conditions is actually small, so they have no choice but to seek the next best thing. However, they ultimately recognize financial resources and credit as a whole, so credit lending is not a moral act of benefiting industry and commerce, but a kind of business of using money wisely. Try asking an experienced qianzhuang expert, and he will not deny it. Because the conditions are not complete, the danger is great. This is why the Legislative Yuan under the Party's rule has taken measures to promulgate laws to restrict it. As for the interpretation of the fourth point, it is thought that Mr. Gu is busy with his pen and has not had time to delve into it, so he has not been able to have a true understanding. According to the Prime Minister's curbing of capital, it is to restrict large capitalists from relying on their financial resources to engage in behaviors that are harmful to society and seek improper profits. The restriction is to restrict its occurrence (originally, the current situation in China is great poverty and small poverty), so the equalization of land rights also stipulates large-scale enterprises, preparing for state-owned operations, and it is not for the financial industry that subsidizes the development of industrial and commercial enterprises in accordance with the principle of people's livelihood to make charitable investments. This is why the Banking Law has measures to restrict credit lending, because it does not violate the doctrine. Moreover, in fact, since it is called industry and commerce, there must be capital. Even if it is as small as a stall or a small shop, it must have capital to operate. It has not been heard that the law allows industrial and commercial organizations without funds to operate in society. As for the suppression of the lives of small and medium-sized merchants, I do not know what your opinion is or what evidence you have. Can credit lending really benefit small workers and small businesses? If there are any, they must belong to the small qianzhuang shops that seek high profits, which is truly contrary to the principle of people's livelihood. Moreover, Article 34 of the Banking Law and the original text of my book all support restriction, not complete abolition. It is hoped that Mr. Gu will pay attention to this point. As for the silkworm cocoon lending in the fifth point, it is purely mortgaged and is a customary practice in the qianzhuang industry. There are also the methods of inner thirty-seven and outer thirty-seven, sending people to supervise and transport the cocoons to the warehouse, and using the bill of lading as a mortgage certificate. The goods never leave the hands of the supervisor for a moment. Who would say that it is not a mortgage? This method has been practiced in the qianzhuang industry for a long time. I think Mr. Gu does not deeply understand the operating methods of the qianzhuang industry. Moreover, there are many types of mortgage lending, and there are also many operating methods that are constantly changing. Unfortunately, I am limited by space and cannot describe them to Mr. Gu.

Letters 179

To the Editor,

Regarding the news in your newspaper on May 14 about the riot of boatmen in Wusong, there is a section stating that Yang Shaozhen, a staff member of the Wusong Shipping Office of this bureau, injured boatman Wang Jinyu with a punt pole. After investigation, Yang Shaozhen was first working on a sand barge when he saw the boatmen rushing over, trapping the small boat of the sand barge, intending to report to the police. Wang Jinyu and others ordered the sand barge to detain Yang Shaozhen. When the people on the boat refused, they fought each other and were injured. At that time, Yang Shaozhen had already swum away. How could he have injured anyone again? The record is inaccurate and confuses the public. Please correct it immediately.

Sincerely,

First Section, Shanghai Public Utilities Bureau, May 14, 20th year.

To the Editor,

Yesterday (May 14th), I read about the incident of Mr. Pan Ruijie encountering bandits in your newspaper's local news, which is completely inconsistent with the facts. On the morning of May 13th, at around 2:00 AM, the director of the First District, Second Precinct of this bureau reported that police officer Sun Yuwang, who was stationed at the New Open River Flour Exchange, reported to the precinct that a car suddenly came to the entrance of the exchange. Three men in suits got out of the car and went straight upstairs. I (the police officer claiming) saw the suspicious appearance and questioned the tea room attendant at the exchange, asking who these three people were. The tea room attendant replied that he did not know. I immediately went forward to question them, but the three men, seeing that someone was questioning them, turned around and got into the car, driving towards the French Concession. After receiving the report, the director immediately sent a patrol officer to investigate. Mr. Pan Ruijie also heard the police and suspected that they were bandits scouting the area. The director praised the police officer Sun Yuwang for his careful service, but it was a pity that he did not record the car's license plate number in a hurry, making it difficult to track. The truth of the matter is only as such. Please correct it in your newspaper to ensure accuracy.

Sincerely,

Shanghai Public Security Bureau, May 14th.

Small World Events 180

—Hai Ke

St. Paul's Cathedral in London. The gold cross on the top of the cathedral faded due to age. It was re-gilded last year. It required 3,000 sheets of 24-karat pure gold leaf, the same as the gold leaf used to decorate Egyptian mummies 4,000 years ago.

American women's handbags. In recent years, they have been particularly enlarged. I once saw a lady's handbag containing a handkerchief, a bundle of letters, a diary, a mirror, a comb, a purse and wallet, a sock mending kit, as well as cigarette cases, lighters, powder cases, lipsticks, keys, shoelaces, and other items. It can be described as a panoramic view.

British aristocrat Mr. Hon. A. E. Guinness recently built an "air yacht" with bedrooms (fully equipped with wardrobes and dressing tables), bathrooms, living rooms, kitchens, etc. It can accommodate six guests and three crew members and can fly 100 miles per hour.

A French engineer has invented a new type of car horn. He installed a sound transmitter in front of the driver. He only needs to say something softly, and it will be amplified and shouted out through the large horn.

London has a large population, and fertility is also increasing daily. According to the 1930 survey, the average number of children born each year is as high as 60,000.

Curves and Straight Lines 181

— Da Mei

Chu Minyi's Lecture on Tai Chi Exercises

On the 11th, I visited a friend at the Soochow University Law School. That day happened to be Monday, and the school held a memorial week. Mr. Chu Minyi, a Central Committee member, came to the school to give a lecture, so I was pestered by my friend to attend and listen to his speech. Mr. Chu, as a Central Committee member, has long been renowned at home for advocating physical education. Recently, he invented the so-called Tai Chi exercises, promoting them tirelessly. His name has also spread overseas. Mr. Chu's lecture at Soochow this time was also on Tai Chi exercises. Some people regard promoting boxing as a minor matter, but they do not know that physical education has a great relationship with national health. In his lectures on nationalism, Dr. Sun Yat-sen also diligently hoped for the health of individuals. Now, I will select the interesting points from Mr. Chu's lecture and record them as follows.

Mr. Chu said that the characteristic of Tai Chi exercises is that the movements of the hands and feet take a circular line instead of a straight line. He believes that the movement of the muscles and bones of the human body is not always confined to front and back. Ordinary gymnastics only focus on straight lines and lack the inner and outer circular twists, which is a defect. After further examination from a mechanical point of view, the superiority of the circular line over the straight line is even more evident. Take a fan as an example. Waving a fan to cool off is a straight line. A step further, people sew a large fan from cloth and hang it in the room, pulling it with a rope. The result is better, but the movement of the fan is still a straight line. When machinery developed, foreigners used electricity to make electric fans. Electric fans have four blades, and their movement no longer takes a straight line but a circular shape. This is one example. In water transportation, there were old sailing ships that used manual oars or paddles. Their movement also took a straight line. When the steam engine came out, wings replaced oars, and they moved around in a circular line. This is the second example. Other examples include airplanes. The principle is actually derived from birds. When birds fly, their wings move up and down, which is also a straight line. However, the wings of airplanes have been changed to take a circular line of rotation, and the results are far better than the flight of birds. This is the third example. Therefore, my Tai Chi exercises take a circular line instead of a straight line.

Mr. Chu also said that people commonly say that those with a short philtrum will not live long. Although there is no scientific basis for this statement, I can prove that there is a good reason for it. The air contains a large amount of dirt and microorganisms, so hygienists often urge people not to breathe through their mouths but to use their noses instead. There is hair in the nose, and the path to the lungs is tortuous and long. During breathing, the dirt and microorganisms in the air are not easy to enter directly. Anyone who breathes through their mouth often opens their mouth wide. The habit of opening the mouth wide causes the upper lip to bend and shorten. The so-called short philtrum is due to this. The dirt and microorganisms in the air can attack the lungs at any time, as if entering a deserted place. It is unlikely that they will not get sick and die early.

Mr. Chu continued to describe the key points of Tai Chi exercises, demonstrating them himself as he spoke. He personally demonstrated them on the podium, as if he were a gymnastics teacher. He had three slogans for promoting Tai Chi exercises: first, it does not take time. The whole set has six sections, which can be completed in more than ten minutes. Second, it does not cost money because no equipment is needed, and no fixed place is required. It can be done anytime, anywhere. Third, it does not take effort. The whole set of movements is light and easy, and both the elderly, children, and women can do it.

After Mr. Chu finished speaking, Mr. Wu Jingxiong, the dean of the Soochow Law School, came forward to give a thank-you speech. Mr. Wu is a follower of Dongfang Shuo. His first sentence at the opening was: I have another word to add to Mr. Chu's reasons for Tai Chi exercises not taking a straight line but a circular line, that is, the circular line has the beauty of a curve. After speaking, he bent his hands up and down, left and right, in the shape of a celestial maiden scattering flowers. There was a burst of laughter in the hall, and everyone dispersed happily.

Chicken Evolution and X-Rays 182

— Qing Deng

Dr. Da Fenbeixi of New York, USA, has taken X-rays of chicken eggs, conducting extremely interesting experiments. This kind of experiment has a great impact on the incubation of chicken eggs and chicks. Most of the chicken eggs are exposed to X-rays, some for only a few minutes, and some for several hours. There are different effects. Those exposed for only a few minutes hatched chicks that were more than 90% female, which is far different from the normal male and female ratio. Those exposed for several hours found a wonderful phenomenon. The chicks hatched were not the same as those of modern times. In the structure of the body, there is a sudden and distinct improvement. According to general scientists, this improvement would require hundreds of years of evolutionary process. But now, after one X-ray, the phenomenon after hundreds of years has suddenly changed. This is amazing.

Old and New Tales of Yangzhou Salt Merchants (Part 2) 183

— Shi Weng

After I left Leping, I worked in Nanjing. One day, I received two telegrams from Yangzhou, saying, "Come quickly." It turned out that Zhang Ziwei, the salt transport commissioner, had summoned me to diagnose his illness. The next day, I took a fast train to Yangzhou and stayed in the Osmanthus Hall of the salt transport commissioner's office. I heard an old man in the office say that the salt transport commissioner's office used to have 999 rooms, but now most of them have collapsed. When Zeng Bingu and Lu Yayu were transport commissioners, all the salt merchants paid tribute every year in addition to their regular salaries, which was a very large amount. Now, it has been reduced by sixty or seventy percent. As for the level of salt administration, the high-handedness, and the internal and external obscurity of the reports, they are regarded as routine and cannot be enumerated. Last year, the Ministry ordered the transport commissioner's office to be moved to Huaibei, and those who relied on the transport commissioner's office to eat suddenly became embarrassed and almost cried and laughed.

In the past, I rented a residence in Wufu Lane in Yangzhou, next to the Geyuan Garden. The owner of Geyuan Garden was named Zhiyun, styled Geyuan, from Ganquan. He was orphaned at the age of fourteen. People seized his inheritance. At the age of nineteen, he rode a donkey to the capital and met a salt administrator of Lianghuai with a letter from his father's friend. He spoke with him and was amazed by his talent. He was regarded as the chief salt merchant of Lianghuai, with the title of salt transport commissioner added to his rank of Dao and Fu. He entered the capital to celebrate the emperor's birthday and was rewarded with listening to a play in the Yuanmingyuan Garden and bestowed with cash. At that time, from the salt administrator to the salt merchants, they all regarded him as a barometer. When people in Yangzhou talked to each other, they would inevitably mention him as the leading figure. He collected thousands of famous paintings and calligraphy, but he did not like music and pleasure. He once went to Su Mei's singing house to invite guests, spending thousands of gold coins a day. People were surprised by his actions. It happened that a Westerner admired him and belonged to transporting more than one million silver, and the report of the sale was obtained as scheduled. His courage and wisdom were indeed unmatched. This can be seen in the biographies of Mei Boyan and Huang Geyuan. In less than a few decades, the family declined day by day. The flowers, trees, pavilions, and rockeries in the garden remain the same. When he died, people entered the room, which is regrettable.

Who is the one who entered the room? It was a salt merchant named Li. He had a rich feast and was arrogant and indulgent. He was frivolous and danced and sang wildly. Passersby looked at him with sideways glances. At that time, there was a poem mocking him: "The moon-white shirt is truly handsome, the water-red hat is suspected to be expensive. The chess pole is erected high behind the door, and the base of the inner room is secretly opened. Most of the time, he sits in the green spring, and the waiter shouts loudly, 'Master is here.'" This is what Mr. Li did when he was alive. After Mr. Li died, the family declined day by day, and only twenty or thirty percent of the Geyuan Garden's buildings remained. The rest were rented out. However, even these twenty or thirty percent are still worth seeing. I and Mr. Yang from Xinghua visited it. Broken stones and scattered monuments, empty pavilions and fallen flowers. I saw two large seal characters on the door plaque: Geyuan Garden. Mr. Li is not worthy of regret, but I am secretly sad for Huang Geyuan. If the new salt law is implemented in the future and taxes are collected on the spot without relying on the lead merchants, I do not know what the tragic situation will be for the sons and grandsons of the lead merchants.

Wax Beauty 184

— Lu Bing

This column often publishes works of art, such as hand-捏 portraits, which are lifelike and become elegant legends. It is admired as an absolute skill. This is what Westerners regard as precious and rare. Recently, according to Mr. Yu, who is studying in France, Paris has rich and famous techniques, and wax beauties are particularly handy and unmatched by other countries. The so-called wax beauties are always displayed in major commercial stores, and occasionally famous ladies in boudoirs or beautiful singers invest in styling for appreciation. Although the forms are of different sizes, the characters are vivid, and viewers often linger and are reluctant to leave. Therefore, I record what I have heard to give a glimpse.

To make a perfect wax beauty, you must first find a model with a beautiful face and a lithe figure. Usually, models are hired for people to describe, and they take off their clothes to reveal the beauty of the body. However, this is not a necessary condition for those hired to make wax figures. What the model should pay attention to is only the beautiful posture. Therefore, experts often provide guidance, teaching various forms to make the whole body beautiful and touching. Then, they focus their eyes and wave their hands, conveying the spirit and describing the shape, forming the negative molds of each part. Those with exquisite skills often do not need to modify them. Once they are matched, it is like a peerless beauty.

The negative mold is made of clay. After it is dry, wax juice is poured into it, leaving a hollow outer contour. After a while, it is moistened with water and removed, and the wax real shape is formed. At this point, there is still important work to be done, such as fitting autumn water pupils into the eye sockets, installing gourd teeth into the oral cavity, and adding delicate operations everywhere to make the eyebrows like black ink and the blue silk like clouds. In this way, the limbs and face are decorated in a fashionable way, and then they are decorated with colors to make the apple cheeks and ice and snow skin complement each other to make a perfect beauty. It is said that the cost of a beauty is at least 50 pounds, and many of the skills are passed down from generation to generation, and ordinary sculptors cannot胜任云.

News from the Publishing World: Li Shiqin's ten proposed life questions have been published in the Shanghai Min Guo Daily by Xu Wancheng to solicit answers, which is quite meaningful. Now it has been printed into a book with the names and mailing lists of the respondents. Send a letter with 15 cents postage to Xu Wancheng, Da Xia Middle School, Jiaozhou Road, Shanghai, and you will receive a copy.

Travels Around the Yellow Sea (3) 185

— Huang Yanpei

Arrived in Dalian on the 21st. It's a place I visited before, but there is one thing that I have never seen before, and I can't help but be shocked. That is the Manchurian-Mongolian Resources Hall established by the South Manchuria Railway Company.

"The South Manchuria Railway Company, under the beautiful name of Japan-China coexistence and co-prosperity, invests more than 440 million in railways, shipping, mines, forests, copper, iron, agriculture, and animal husbandry in its territory. Although the name is semi-official and semi-private, the actual power is controlled by the government, giving it diplomatic police and general political power, allowing it to exert imperialism and form a special society, no different from the second Korean unification." These few sentences are not my speculation but are from the memorial of the late Tanaka Cabinet of Japan, as seen in the Current Affairs Monthly in December of the 18th year of the Republic. It is the Japanese government's own供状.

As soon as you enter the Resources Hall, there is a large piece of coal, taller than a person by half a body, with commensurate width and thickness. It was obtained from the open-pit excavation of Fushun.

The mineral products department occupies one-fourth of the entire hall, agricultural and forestry products occupy one-fourth, animal husbandry occupies one-fourth, and another fourth is the geological survey institute.

Each department has a large map of important product producing areas and a large statistical chart of production. The mineral products room has a large map model of Manchuria and Mongolia, with electric lights indicating the location and production of important mineral products. Each product has a detailed explanation.

Japan does not produce iron. The steel used is imported from the Yangtze River basin and the Malay Peninsula in Southeast Asia. They estimate that the proven reserves of iron in South Manchuria are at least 1.2 billion tons. What is even more valuable is that the estimated reserves of coal in the same place, such as Fushun, Benxi, and Xinqiu, are 250 million tons, which is enough to refine 1.2 billion tons of steel for Japan's needs for 70 years. The Anshan Iron and Steel Plant currently produces 200,000 tons of iron per year. The Benxihu Iron and Steel Plant produces 120,000 tons of iron per year. Fushun produces more than 7.4 million tons of coal per year. Benxihu produces 500,000 tons of coal per year. Yantai in Liaoyang County produces 100,000 tons of coal per year. Other places are not listed.
