The Hawthorne Detective Case Turning Point (14) 186

— Cheng Xiaoqing

(5) My Disappointment

We left the fourth precinct. Hawthorne drove me home. In the car, we re-discussed this issue. I said to Hawthorne, "This person is really insidious and hateful. If we can't find him and give him a proper retribution, it would be a great shame for us. Imagine what kind of people we will be seen as if he talks about it in front of friends." Hawthorne nodded and said, "Yes, but the outcome of things lies in the last move. Don't worry for now. I think this time we suffered a loss, it won't just end here." I said, "This time, this person used his intelligence and deception to fool us. I guess he must be our enemy. He must have suffered a loss from us somewhere before, and now he is planning revenge. What do you think?" Hawthorne lowered his head and slowly replied, "Of course, this is a very possible understanding." I said, "In this way, it may not be a clue. We can just look for it from the letter." I said this and immediately stopped. I felt that my words were too vague. How many enemies do we have? Can we know ourselves? In which case did the enemy in front of us结怨? How can we think of it? Fortunately, Hawthorne seemed to be thinking deeply there. He seemed not to have heard my words. He pondered for a while before looking up and saying, "I think there is another reason besides revenge—wait a minute. Isn't this person you have seen with your own eyes?" I replied, "Exactly. If I see him again, I will definitely be able to identify him." Hawthorne said, "Then, when you were at Gao's house, did you ever see this person, for example, did he sit at the same table with someone, or did he approach someone? Can you still recall it?" I shook my head repeatedly and said, "I didn't pay attention at all. I'm not even sure if I saw this person at Gao's house." Hawthorne paused and asked me again, "Then, tell me what kind of clothes this person was wearing." I said, "He was wearing a gray spring tweed coat with a plaid pattern and a dark brown bowler hat on his head." Hawthorne frowned and said, "Didn't you see the clothes inside?" I said, "I saw them. He was wearing a chestnut-colored pair of pants." Hawthorne stopped his gaze again and lowered his head to think. I continued, "His figure is similar to mine, but his shoulders don't seem to be as broad as mine."

Grain. Local Street Sales Brisk for Ke Xian Rice.

Yesterday, the Ke Xian rice market was active, because the local street was very active in handling inventories. Foreign rice was dumped again, and foreign firms sold it. The overall trading volume was high, and the market situation has greatly improved. The Ke Xian rice is unified by the local street. The reason why the local street's inventory is strong is because the supply of rice from the lower reaches of the river is lacking, and the sales are brisk. Therefore, we are paying attention to the Ke Xian rice. The Ke Xian rice has a small stock and lacks supply. Once the local street sells smoothly, the market price should rise. The foreign firms have repeatedly dumped foreign rice in the past few days, and the merchants have no transactions, so although the situation is good, the price has not risen. Noodle Prices Rose with the Rain 194

The bulls took advantage of the situation to raise prices

Yesterday's noodle market, after opening in the morning, the market for each month, because the price of foreign wheat was small, about 12 cents, and the weather was still clear, so the market for each month was not stable. However, because the mainland gangs were still aggressively entering, the market sentiment turned firm again. When the afternoon market opened, the weather suddenly changed, and there was light rain. The latent market sentiment was unusually excited. The buyers from the mainland gangs did not limit the price and entered smoothly in each market. After the third market, because the rain was heavier, the speculative bulls also took the opportunity to raise the price, causing the buying price to become more and more excited, and the market showed a skyrocketing trend. This month's market is still flat because of the sluggish actual sales and the merchants returning. Otherwise, the increase should be more serious. As a result, this month was up 2 fen 2 li 5 compared to the previous day, June was up 4 fen 2 li 5, July was up 4.5 fen, August was up 4 fen 2 li 5, September was up 4 fen, and October was up 3 fen 7 li 5.

The Wheat Futures Market Made Great Progress 195

Purely Affected by the Impact of the Rain

Yesterday's wheat futures market, after opening in the morning, the market for each month, because the price of foreign wheat turned small, and the weather was also good as usual, so the market situation for each month was generally stable, with very little fluctuation. When the afternoon market opened, the market atmosphere for each month suddenly changed greatly. Because it suddenly rained when the market opened, the buyers from the mainland gangs suddenly made aggressive entries. The general empty positions were also scrambling to make up for it. Later, it was reported that the flour market was greatly raised, and the buying atmosphere inside and outside the industry became more and more intense, causing each month to show a surge. After observing the subsequent steps, if the sky does not clear up, the increase is afraid that it will not be finished. As a result, this month was up 5 fen compared to the previous day, June was up 6 fen, July was up 9 fen, August was up 1 qian 1 fen, and September and October were up 1 qian.

Silk and Tea. European and American Silk Sales More Clear.

Although the Bai factory had a telegram from overseas, the exchange rate shrank and the price was small, making it more and more flat and tired. Yesterday, Dachan entered 10 packages of Shanghai Bai factory, Boxing and others entered 15 packages of Huang Yaojing, Sanxing and others entered 20 packages of Huang coarse silk, and the price was difficult to increase.

Yiwu Spring Silkworms Are Going to Mount and Make Cocoons 196

Bad Weather, Most Abandoned ... Only 30% of Those That Mounted

Yiwu County has the earliest silkworm season in various cities and villages. The early silkworms raised by farmers this year were completely abandoned. The late silkworms are still developing unfavorably due to the cold and rainy weather. In addition, in the middle of the big sleep, the big rain lasted for ten days, and the weather was extremely cold. Silkworm diseases broke out, such as diarrhea, yellow, black, red stiff, white stiff, etc., and 70% of them were abandoned. There are not many remaining silkworms, and they are now going to mount and make cocoons. Each cocoon line will be priced on the 18th. Because the current situation is like this, the cocoon production is bound to be limited. Therefore, there will be no more than one or two cocoon lines that will collect the cocoons.

Wenzhou's New Red Tea Officially Opens for Trading 197

Yesterday, a small amount of new red tea from Wenzhou arrived on the market. British firms Jardine Matheson and Ewo were exceptionally interested. After several rounds of negotiations, the opening price was set at 52 taels, which is 10 taels higher than last year and an unprecedentedly high price. As for the new green tea produced by local tea factories, the market remained quiet yesterday. Although some tea merchants displayed new samples of "Zhen Mei" tea from Huzhou and Sui'an, the prices offered by foreign firms were 10 to 20 taels lower than before. At this crucial time when new tea is entering the market, Chinese tea merchants, considering their costs, are unwilling to excessively lower prices to sell. The green tea market is showing a stalemate.

Book Review

The Marriage Problem in China 198

— Tang Bin

"The Marriage Problem" is an extremely important one among the three major problems of life. It has become one that urgently needs to be resolved in every country. However, human affairs are never simple, and the things that are most urgent to resolve often end up being the things that can never be resolved. This has become a common pattern. In any country, specialized books on the marriage problem occupy a major position in bookstores. Moreover, in great and famous literary and artistic works, as well as in films and dramas, the urgency of marriage is always expressed in the important aspects of their content. The reason for this is, of course, very simple. As the author states in the introduction, "From a vertical perspective, due to changes in customs or culture, the marriage system has undergone many transformations. From a horizontal perspective, due to the complex relationships between individual personalities and social environments, it is not easy to achieve satisfactory results in marriage and divorce, and it is often impossible. Therefore, the marriage problem not only occupies a major position among social problems in various countries but also seems to be a problem that can never be solved."

This statement is indeed very appropriate. Especially in Chinese society, we only need to pay attention to the major newspapers and periodicals published daily to know that the problem of unsatisfactory marriage resolutions can be found everywhere. The main reason for this is that in recent decades, after China opened up to the world, new European culture was formally introduced, causing significant changes to the inherent culture. Until the outbreak of the May Fourth Movement, both the old and new systems were caught in contradictions. During this transitional period, various social problems naturally became urgent and demanded resolution. Therefore, the marriage problem became the most urgent problem that needed to be resolved. Thus, "The cry to resolve the marriage problem has risen like an angry tide, spreading across the country. In recent years, after the high tide of the National Revolution swept across the country, new standards have gradually been established. However, the old standards are still striving to exist. Therefore, the urgency of the marriage problem is increasing daily and without end." Since the marriage problem is so important, Chinese scholars, in general, do not pay attention to it. They are even afraid to speak about this issue concerning men and women. Professor Zhang Weici expresses this very clearly, saying,

"Chinese scholars talk about 'nature' and 'reason' all day long. They are very solemn and respectful figures, putting on serious faces, writing their books, spreading their doctrines, and establishing their words. As for the most essential problem of life, the problem of men and women, they do not talk about it. Foreign scholars are not like this. They are willing to talk about anything and any phenomenon, and the words they speak are superior, often able to say what others cannot or dare not say. Regarding problems such as men and women, marriage, and love, they indeed have many profound sayings. Although sometimes their words may be a bit too excessive, they are all spoken from the heart. Their point of view is very special. They can indeed honestly think in their hearts and write in their pens what they think, unlike our Chinese moralists who are full of benevolence and morality in front of people but do anything behind their backs. What they write is completely different from what they think in their hearts." The author of this book, aware of this point, has formed a noteworthy monograph discussing the marriage problem in China. The entire book is divided into eleven chapters, which are analyzed below:

Chapter 1, the Introduction, explains the various reasons for the urgency of the marriage problem, from the improved status of women under the Kuomintang rule, demanding the same equality as men, unwilling to be oppressed by traditional ethics, and even more unwilling to be oppressed by men. However, there is no love in Chinese marriages. In the past, most people simply did not know what "love" was or what marriage was, so there were no problems. In recent years, most young people have realized that loveless marriages are no longer acceptable and cannot be tolerated. As a result, open social interactions between men and women have suddenly begun. Therefore, many conflicting phenomena have arisen in society, with some being forced into "loveless marriages" and others "in love but unable to marry." In this way, the urgency of the marriage problem in China has been brewing. Moreover, Chinese society opposes divorce. Once a couple is married, they are not allowed to separate, regardless of whether the marriage is good or bad. Many of the divorce cases and self-immolation problems that have arisen in recent years have been largely caused by this. Finally, China also has a so-called extended family system, which only cares about the interests of the family and does not pay attention to the happiness of individual marriages, thus hindering the true happiness of individuals and their loved ones. Through this detailed description, the author demonstrates the urgency of the marriage problem in China. As for the content of the marriage problem, it generally includes problems before and after marriage. The problem before marriage is engagement, which includes the conditions of engagement, the issue of parental authority, the legal requirements for engagement and its cancellation, and various engagement ceremonies. The problems after marriage include the wedding ceremony, the maintenance of love and discord between husband and wife, the surname of children, the surname of the husband and wife, as well as divorce, separation, abandonment, remarriage, and so on. Regarding these, those who study social problems need to pay attention, but they should focus on facts rather than relying solely on ideals. Here, the author has systematically collected materials on marriage records, covering the various issues mentioned above, which can also be used as historical reference.

Chapter 2, The Meaning of Marriage and the Conditions of Engagement, describes the general misunderstanding of marriage in China. People do not value marriage. The so-called "major event of marriage" is nothing more than "Marriage is for inheriting the family business and continuing the lineage." This can be said to be a historical flaw in our nation.

Page 22

Originally, in any country, as long as a "patriarchal family" still exists in its history, the happiness of the children does not need to be questioned. In China, although parents in the past valued the marriages of their children, the practice of first issuing commands and then arranging matches through matchmakers was fundamentally wrong. Here, the author wants to discuss what the true meaning of marriage is. He has conducted detailed research on the way of love and also explains how to get engaged. The union of two sexes should be entirely based on love, and there should be no conditions for engagement. Although this is the theory, there are many conditions in reality. The author analyzes them objectively, which is worthy of our study. How children should cope with their environment and how parents should deal with their children's marriages are also discussed. Chapter 3, The Wedding Ceremony, starts from the so-called "Six Rites" of ancient China to the modern wedding ceremony. It explores a better ceremony to assist those getting married. In the author's opinion, it is advocated to use the "advertisement or written notice method," followed by a "celebratory tea party," which is the most economical and suitable method for modern society.

Chapter 4, Maintaining and Destroying Love, provides an explanation for the complex situation between couples. "The secret to maintaining love" is a section worth noting. Secondly, how to deal with a wife without love is discussed. In order to seek lifelong happiness, one should not succumb to the old environment of China. Furthermore, chastity is also one of the important issues in the marriage problem.

Chapter 5, Early Marriage and Late Marriage, explains their advantages and disadvantages and provides illustrations of the legal marriage ages in various countries, which is of great significance. Before the complete promulgation of the Chinese Civil Code, there were naturally no regulations on the marriage age. However, the legal marriage ages in previous dynasties are also listed in detail. This kind of comparative study clarifies the "appropriate marriage age."

Chapter 6, Variant Marriages, refers to Chinese marriages, which, in addition to ordinary marriages, also have many variant marriages, such as sons-in-law who move into the bride's family, marriages arranged before birth, child brides, women who become widows before marriage, remarriage, bigamy, dual-household and concurrent inheritance. Concubinage was originally also a variant marriage, but now the law does not recognize concubinage as a form of marriage, so the author has listed it as a separate chapter and does not discuss it in detail here.

Chapter 6, The Issue of Concubinage, is extremely important. At the recent National Conference, there was a proposal on this issue, indicating that the concubinage system is currently an urgent problem that needs to be resolved. The author describes it from a historical perspective in China, commenting on the concubinage system, the issue of descendants, and its remedies. A diagram of the concubine's mourning attire for the head of the family and clan is also provided for reference.

Chapter 8, The Issue of Divorce, has become one of the most common phenomena in modern society. The author starts from the theoretical basis of divorce, using the "Seven Grounds for Divorce and Three Exceptions" as the legal basis for interpretation, and the "Chinese Divorce Law" is based on the draft of the Civil Code. Two attitudes are taken towards divorce: (1) divorce by agreement between husband and wife, and (2) legal restrictions on divorce. These are explained in detail in this chapter.

Chapter 9, Marriage and Law, Chapter 10, Solving the Marriage Problem, and Chapter 11, Afterthoughts, are all value theories of the marriage problem, which can serve as our compass for exploration.

According to the author, this book, although he dares not say that it contains profound insights on the marriage problem, can be said to be written with what he thinks in his heart and what he writes in his pen. Perhaps there are one or two things that others cannot say or dare not say. At least, there are some things that moralists cannot say or dare not say. What is great about this book is this point, and what modern readers with scientific minds need is also this point.

Manuscript Guidelines for Book Reviews 199

(1) The text should be limited to introducing new publications from home and abroad. Apart from literary works, all books and newspapers on politics, economics, law, science, education, etc., are eligible for review. However, frivolous books and newspapers will not be reviewed.

(2) Pictures should be limited to recent works by new artists from home and abroad and related illustrations that are relevant to the text.

(3) Articles on textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(4) Pictures and photos should be limited to those related to the text.

(5) The text should not exceed 3,000 characters.

(6) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw pictures, and do not use colored paper. White paper and black ink must be used.

(8) Please indicate "Book Review Editor" on the submitted manuscript.

(9) Submitted manuscripts will not be returned regardless of whether they are published or not. If a return is required, please state so in advance and attach sufficient postage.

(10) Remuneration for text is 3 yuan, 2 yuan, or 1 yuan per thousand characters, in three categories. The same applies to pictures and photos. If there are special manuscripts, the remuneration will be calculated separately.
